Changes in the way we use land; the expansion and intensification of agriculture; and unsustainable trade, production and consumption disrupt nature and increase contact between wildlife, livestock, pathogens and people. This is the path to pandemics."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPBESPandemic_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-IPBESPandemic-230">[230]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Conservation">Conservation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Conservation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Conservation_biology" title="Conservation biology">Conservation biology</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MEAConservationStrategies.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1398" data-file-width="1398" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/MEAConservationStrategies.jpg/220px-MEAConservationStrategies.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/MEAConservationStrategies.jpg/330px-MEAConservationStrategies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/MEAConservationStrategies.jpg/440px-MEAConservationStrategies.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MEAConservationStrategies.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A schematic image illustrating the relationship between biodiversity, ecosystem services, human well-being and poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup> The illustration shows where conservation action, strategies, and plans can influence the drivers of the current biodiversity crisis at local, regional, to global scales.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gletscherschmelze.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="519" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Gletscherschmelze.jpg/300px-Gletscherschmelze.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Gletscherschmelze.jpg/450px-Gletscherschmelze.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Gletscherschmelze.jpg/600px-Gletscherschmelze.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gletscherschmelze.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Retreat_of_glaciers_since_1850" title="Retreat of glaciers since 1850">retreat</a> of <a href="/wiki/Aletsch_Glacier" title="Aletsch Glacier">Aletsch Glacier</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Alps" title="Swiss Alps">Swiss Alps</a> (situation in 1979, 1991 and 2002), due to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a>.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Conservation_biology" title="Conservation biology">Conservation biology</a> matured in the mid-20th century as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecologists" title="Ecologists">ecologists</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naturalists" title="Naturalists">naturalists</a> and other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scientists" title="Scientists">scientists</a> began to research and address issues pertaining to global biodiversity declines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Soule86_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-Soule86-232">[232]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davis96_233-0"><a href="#cite_note-Davis96-233">[233]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dyke2008_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dyke2008-234">[234]</a></sup>
</p><p>The conservation ethic advocates management of <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">natural resources</a> for the purpose of sustaining biodiversity in <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecosystems" title="Ecosystems">ecosystems</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">evolutionary process</a> and human culture and society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-proceedings1_217-1"><a href="#cite_note-proceedings1-217">[217]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Soule86_232-1"><a href="#cite_note-Soule86-232">[232]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dyke2008_234-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dyke2008-234">[234]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hunter1996_235-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hunter1996-235">[235]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup>
</p><p>Conservation biology is reforming around strategic plans to protect biodiversity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Soule86_232-2"><a href="#cite_note-Soule86-232">[232]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Soulé1986_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-Soulé1986-237">[237]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup> Preserving global biodiversity is a priority in strategic conservation plans that are designed to engage public policy and concerns affecting local, regional and global scales of communities, ecosystems and cultures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> Action plans identify <a href="/wiki/Ecological_economics#Methodology" title="Ecological economics">ways</a> of sustaining human well-being, employing <a href="/wiki/Natural_capital" title="Natural capital">natural capital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capital_market" title="Capital market">market capital</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecosystem_services" title="Ecosystem services">ecosystem services</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=EU_Directive_1999/22/EC&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="EU Directive 1999/22/EC (page does not exist)">EU Directive 1999/22/EC</a> zoos are described as having a role in the preservation of the biodiversity of wildlife animals by conducting research or participation in <a href="/wiki/Breeding_program" title="Breeding program">breeding programs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Protection_and_restoration_techniques">Protection and restoration techniques</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Protection and restoration techniques">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Removal of exotic species will allow the species that they have negatively impacted to recover their ecological niches. Exotic species that have become pests can be identified taxonomically (e.g., with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Digital_Automated_Identification_SYstem" title="Digital Automated Identification SYstem">Digital Automated Identification SYstem</a> (DAISY), using the <a href="/wiki/Consortium_for_the_Barcode_of_Life" title="Consortium for the Barcode of Life">barcode of life</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup> Removal is practical only given large groups of individuals due to the economic cost.
</p><p>As sustainable populations of the remaining native species in an area become assured, "missing" species that are candidates for reintroduction can be identified using databases such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclopedia_of_Life#Resources_and_collaborations" title="Encyclopedia of Life">Encyclopedia of Life</a></i> and the <a href="/wiki/Global_Biodiversity_Information_Facility" title="Global Biodiversity Information Facility">Global Biodiversity Information Facility</a>.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_banking" title="Biodiversity banking">Biodiversity banking</a> places a monetary value on biodiversity. One example is the Australian <a href="/wiki/Native_Vegetation_Management_Framework" title="Native Vegetation Management Framework">Native Vegetation Management Framework</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gene_bank" title="Gene bank">Gene banks</a> are collections of specimens and genetic material. Some banks intend to reintroduce banked species to the ecosystem (e.g., via tree nurseries).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup></li>
<li>Reduction and better targeting of pesticides allows more species to survive in agricultural and urbanized areas.</li>
<li>Location-specific approaches may be less useful for protecting migratory species. One approach is to create <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_corridor" title="Wildlife corridor">wildlife corridors</a> that correspond to the animals' movements. National and other boundaries can complicate corridor creation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Protected_areas">Protected areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Protected areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Protected areas, including forest reserves and biosphere reserves, serve many functions including for affording protection to wild animals and their habitat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup> Protected areas have been set up all over the world with the specific aim of protecting and conserving plants and animals. Some scientists have called on the global community to designate as protected areas of 30 percent of the planet by 2030, and 50 percent by 2050, in order to mitigate biodiversity loss from anthropogenic causes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup> In a study published 4 September 2020 in <a href="/wiki/Science_Advances" title="Science Advances">Science Advances</a> researchers mapped out regions that can help meet critical conservation and climate goals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup>
</p><p>
Protected areas safeguard nature and cultural resources and contribute to livelihoods, particularly at local level. There are over 238 563 designated protected areas worldwide, equivalent to 14.9 percent of the earth's land surface, varying in their extension, level of protection, and type of management (IUCN, 2018).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Percentage_of_forest_in_legally_protected_areas,_2020.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="353" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Percentage_of_forest_in_legally_protected_areas%2C_2020.svg/220px-Percentage_of_forest_in_legally_protected_areas%2C_2020.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Percentage_of_forest_in_legally_protected_areas%2C_2020.svg/330px-Percentage_of_forest_in_legally_protected_areas%2C_2020.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Percentage_of_forest_in_legally_protected_areas%2C_2020.svg/440px-Percentage_of_forest_in_legally_protected_areas%2C_2020.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Percentage_of_forest_in_legally_protected_areas,_2020.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Percentage of forest in legally protected areas, 2020, from the <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a> publication The State of the World's Forests 2020. Forests, biodiversity and people – In brief<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_31-3"><a href="#cite_note-:7-31">[31]</a></sup></div></div></div><p>Forest protected areas are a subset of all protected areas in which a significant portion of the area is forest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_23-3"><a href="#cite_note-:8-23">[23]</a></sup> This may be the whole or only a part of the protected area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_23-4"><a href="#cite_note-:8-23">[23]</a></sup> Globally, 18 percent of the world's forest area, or more than 700 million hectares, fall within legally established protected areas such as national parks, conservation areas and game reserves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_23-5"><a href="#cite_note-:8-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>The benefits of protected areas extend beyond their immediate environment and time. In addition to conserving nature, protected areas are crucial for securing the long-term delivery of ecosystem services. They provide numerous benefits including the conservation of genetic resources for food and agriculture, the provision of medicine and health benefits, the provision of water, recreation and tourism, and for acting as a buffer against disaster. Increasingly, there is acknowledgement of the wider socioeconomic values of these natural ecosystems and of the ecosystem services they can provide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup>
</p><p>Forest protected areas in particular play many important roles including as a provider of habitat, shelter, food and genetic materials, and as a buffer against disaster. They deliver stable supplies of many goods and environmental services.  The role of protected areas, especially forest protected areas, in mitigating and adapting to climate change has increasingly been recognized over the last few years. Protected areas not only store and sequester carbon (i.e. the global network of protected areas stores at least 15 percent of terrestrial carbon), but also enable species to adapt to changing climate patterns by providing refuges and migration corridors. Protected areas also protect people from sudden climate events and reduce their vulnerability to weather-induced problems such as floods and droughts (UNEP–WCMC, 2016).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_parks">National parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: National parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">National park</a></div>
<p>National park is a large natural or near natural areas set aside to protect large-scale ecological processes, which also provide a foundation for environmentally and culturally compatible, spiritual, scientific, educational, recreational and visitor opportunities. These areas are selected by governments or private organizations to protect natural biodiversity along with its underlying ecological structure and supporting environmental processes, and to promote education and recreation. The <a href="/wiki/International_Union_for_Conservation_of_Nature" title="International Union for Conservation of Nature">International Union for Conservation of Nature</a> (IUCN), and its World Commission on Protected Areas (WCPA), has defined "National Park" as its Category II type of protected areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup>
</p><p>National parks are usually owned and managed by national or state governments. In some cases, a limit is placed on the number of visitors permitted to enter certain fragile areas. Designated trails or roads are created. The visitors are allowed to enter only for study, cultural and recreation purposes. Forestry operations, grazing of animals and hunting of animals are regulated and the exploitation of habitat or wildlife is banned.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife_sanctuary">Wildlife sanctuary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Wildlife sanctuary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wildlife_sanctuary" title="Wildlife sanctuary">Wildlife sanctuaries</a> aim only at the conservation of species and have the following features:
</p>
<ol><li>The boundaries of the sanctuaries are not limited by state legislation.</li>
<li>The killing, hunting or capturing of any species is prohibited except by or under the control of the highest authority in the department which is responsible for the management of the sanctuary.</li>
<li>Private ownership may be allowed.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">Forestry</a> and other usages can also be permitted.</li></ol>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Forest_reserves">Forest reserves</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Forest reserves">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There is an estimated 726 million ha of forest in protected areas worldwide. Of the six major world regions, South America has the highest share of forests in protected areas, 31 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Forest" title="Forest">forests</a> play a vital role in harboring more than 45,000 floral and 81,000 faunal species of which 5150 floral and 1837 faunal species are <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup> In addition, there are 60,065 different tree species in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup> Plant and animal species confined to a specific geographical area are called endemic species. In forest reserves, rights to activities like hunting and grazing are sometimes given to communities living on the fringes of the forest, who sustain their livelihood partially or wholly from forest resources or products. The unclassed forests cover 6.4 percent of the total forest area and they are marked by the following characteristics:
</p>
<ol><li>They are large inaccessible forests.</li>
<li>Many of these are unoccupied.</li>
<li>They are ecologically and economically less important.</li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Steps_to_conserve_the_forest_cover">Steps to conserve the forest cover</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Steps to conserve the forest cover">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Forest_cover" title="Forest cover">Forest cover</a></div>
<ol><li>An extensive <a href="/wiki/Reforestation" title="Reforestation">reforestation</a>/<a href="/wiki/Afforestation" title="Afforestation">afforestation</a> programme should be followed.</li>
<li>Alternative <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environment-friendly" title="Environment-friendly">environment-friendly</a> sources of fuel energy such as <a href="/wiki/Biogas" title="Biogas">biogas</a> other than wood should be used.</li>
<li>Loss of biodiversity due to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forest_fire" title="Forest fire">forest fire</a> is a major problem, immediate steps to prevent forest fire need to be taken.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Overgrazing" title="Overgrazing">Overgrazing</a> by cattle can damage a forest seriously. Therefore, certain steps should be taken to prevent overgrazing by cattle.</li>
<li>Hunting and <a href="/wiki/Poaching" title="Poaching">poaching</a> should be banned.</li></ol>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zoological_parks">Zoological parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Zoological parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zoological_park" title="Zoological park">zoological parks</a> or zoos, live animals are kept for public <a href="/wiki/Recreation" title="Recreation">recreation</a>, education and conservation purposes. Modern zoos offer veterinary facilities, provide opportunities for threatened species to <a href="/wiki/Captive_breeding" title="Captive breeding">breed in captivity</a> and usually build environments that simulate the native habitats of the animals in their care. Zoos play a major role in creating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_awareness" title="Environmental awareness">awareness</a> about the need to conserve nature.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Botanical_gardens">Botanical gardens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Botanical gardens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical gardens</a>, plants are grown and displayed primarily for scientific and educational purposes. They consist of a collection of living plants, grown outdoors or under glass in <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse" title="Greenhouse">greenhouses</a> and conservatories. Also, a botanical garden may include a collection of dried plants or <a href="/wiki/Herbarium" title="Herbarium">herbarium</a> and such facilities as lecture rooms, laboratories, libraries, museums and experimental or research plantings.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Resource_allocation">Resource allocation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Resource allocation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Focusing on limited areas of higher potential biodiversity promises greater immediate return on investment than spreading resources evenly or focusing on areas of little diversity but greater interest in biodiversity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup>
</p><p>A second strategy focuses on areas that retain most of their original diversity, which typically require little or no restoration. These are typically non-urbanized, non-agricultural areas. Tropical areas often fit both criteria, given their natively high diversity and relative lack of development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_society">In society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: In society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Decision-making" title="Decision-making">Decision-making</a> and <a href="/wiki/Resource_allocation" title="Resource allocation">Resource allocation</a></div>
<p>In September 2020 scientists reported that "immediate efforts, consistent with the broader <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainability</a> agenda but of unprecedented ambition and <a href="/wiki/Governance" title="Governance">coordination</a>, could enable the provision of <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">food</a> for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_population_growth" title="Human population growth">growing human population</a> while reversing the global terrestrial biodiversity trends caused by <a href="/wiki/Habitat_conservation" title="Habitat conservation">habitat conversion</a>" and recommend measures such as for addressing drivers of <a href="/wiki/Land_use,_land-use_change,_and_forestry" title="Land use, land-use change, and forestry">land-use change</a>, and for increasing the extent of land under <a href="/wiki/Conservation_management_system" title="Conservation management system">conservation management</a>, efficiency in <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_agriculture" title="Sustainable agriculture">agriculture</a> and the shares of <a href="/wiki/Plant-based_diet" title="Plant-based diet">plant-based diets</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Citizen_science">Citizen science</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Citizen science">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Citizen_science" title="Citizen science">Citizen science</a>, also known as public participation in scientific research, has been widely used in environmental sciences and is particularly popular in a biodiversity-related context. It has been used to enable scientists to involve the general public in biodiversity research, thereby enabling the scientists to collect data that they would otherwise not have been able to obtain. An online survey of 1,160 CS participants across 63 biodiversity citizen science projects in Europe, Australia and New Zealand reported positive changes in (a) content, process and nature of science knowledge, (b) skills of science inquiry, (c) self-efficacy for science and the environment, (d) interest in science and the environment, (e) motivation for science and the environment and (f) behaviour towards the environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup>
</p><p>Volunteer observers have made significant contributions to on-the-ground knowledge about biodiversity, and recent improvements in technology have helped increase the flow and quality of occurrences from citizen sources. A 2016 study published in Biological Conservation<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup> registers the massive contributions that citizen scientists already make to data mediated by the <a href="/wiki/Global_Biodiversity_Information_Facility" title="Global Biodiversity Information Facility">Global Biodiversity Information Facility (GBIF)</a>. Despite some limitations of the dataset-level analysis, it's clear that nearly half of all occurrence records shared through the GBIF network come from datasets with significant volunteer contributions. Recording and sharing observations are enabled by several global-scale platforms, including <a href="/wiki/INaturalist" title="INaturalist">iNaturalist</a> and <a href="/wiki/EBird" title="EBird">eBird</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_status">Legal status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Legal status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hopetoun_falls.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Hopetoun_falls.jpg/220px-Hopetoun_falls.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Hopetoun_falls.jpg/330px-Hopetoun_falls.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Hopetoun_falls.jpg/440px-Hopetoun_falls.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hopetoun_falls.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A great deal of work is occurring to preserve the natural characteristics of <a href="/wiki/Hopetoun_Falls" title="Hopetoun Falls">Hopetoun Falls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> while continuing to allow visitor access.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International">International</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: International">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>United Nations <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Biological_Diversity" title="Convention on Biological Diversity">Convention on Biological Diversity</a> (1992) and <a href="/wiki/Cartagena_Protocol_on_Biosafety" title="Cartagena Protocol on Biosafety">Cartagena Protocol on Biosafety</a>;</li>
<li>Convention on International Trade in Endangered Species (<a href="/wiki/CITES" title="CITES">CITES</a>);</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ramsar_Convention" title="Ramsar Convention">Ramsar Convention</a> (Wetlands);</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bonn_Convention" title="Bonn Convention">Bonn Convention</a> on Migratory Species;</li>
<li>United Nations <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site#Convention_and_background" title="World Heritage Site">Convention concerning the Protection of the World's Cultural and Natural Heritage</a> (indirectly by protecting biodiversity habitats)</li>
<li>Regional Conventions such as the Apia Convention</li>
<li>Bilateral agreements such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japan-Australia_Migratory_Bird_Agreement" title="Japan-Australia Migratory Bird Agreement">Japan-Australia Migratory Bird Agreement</a>.</li></ul>
<p>Global agreements such as the <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Biological_Diversity" title="Convention on Biological Diversity">Convention on Biological Diversity</a>, give "sovereign national rights over biological resources" (not property). The agreements commit countries to "conserve biodiversity", "develop resources for sustainability" and "share the benefits" resulting from their use. Biodiverse countries that allow <a href="/wiki/Bioprospecting" title="Bioprospecting">bioprospecting</a> or collection of natural products, expect a share of the benefits rather than allowing the individual or institution that discovers/exploits the resource to capture them privately. Bioprospecting can become a type of <a href="/wiki/Biopiracy" title="Biopiracy">biopiracy</a> when such principles are not respected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup>
</p><p>Sovereignty principles can rely upon what is better known as <a href="/wiki/International_Treaty_on_Plant_Genetic_Resources_for_Food_and_Agriculture" title="International Treaty on Plant Genetic Resources for Food and Agriculture">Access and Benefit Sharing Agreements</a> (ABAs). The Convention on Biodiversity implies <a href="/wiki/Informed_consent" title="Informed consent">informed consent</a> between the source country and the collector, to establish which resource will be used and for what and to settle on a <a href="/wiki/International_Treaty_on_Plant_Genetic_Resources_for_Food_and_Agriculture" title="International Treaty on Plant Genetic Resources for Food and Agriculture">fair agreement on benefit sharing</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Union">European Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: European Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In May 2020, the European Union published its Biodiversity Strategy for 2030. The biodiversity strategy is an essential part of the <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation" title="Climate change mitigation">climate change mitigation</a> strategy of the European Union. From the 25% of the European budget that will go to fight climate change, large part will go to restore biodiversity and <a href="/wiki/Nature-based_solutions" title="Nature-based solutions">nature based solutions</a>.
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU_Biodiversity_Strategy_for_2030" title="EU Biodiversity Strategy for 2030">EU Biodiversity Strategy for 2030</a> include the next targets:
</p>
<ul><li>Protect 30% of the sea territory and 30% of the land territory especially <a href="/wiki/Old-growth_forest" title="Old-growth forest">Old-growth forests</a>.</li>
<li>Plant 3 billion trees by 2030.</li>
<li>Restore at least 25,000 kilometers of rivers, so they will become free flowing.</li>
<li>Reduce the use of <a href="/wiki/Pesticide" title="Pesticide">Pesticides</a> by 50% by 2030.</li>
<li>Increase <a href="/wiki/Organic_farming" title="Organic farming">Organic farming</a>. In linked EU program <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=From_Farm_to_Fork&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="From Farm to Fork (page does not exist)">From Farm to Fork</a> it is said, that the target is making 25% of EU agriculture organic, by 2030.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup></li>
<li>Increase <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biodiverisity_in_agriculture" title="Biodiverisity in agriculture">Biodiverisity in agriculture</a>.</li>
<li>Give €20 billion per year to the issue and make it part of the business practice.</li></ul>
<p>Approximately half of the global <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GDP" title="GDP">GDP</a> depend on nature. In Europe many parts of the economy that generate trillions of euros per year depend on nature. The benefits of <a href="/wiki/Natura_2000" title="Natura 2000">Natura 2000</a> alone in Europe are €200 – €300 billion per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_level_laws">National level laws</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: National level laws">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Biodiversity is taken into account in some political and judicial decisions:
</p>
<ul><li>The relationship between law and ecosystems is very ancient and has consequences for biodiversity. It is related to private and public property rights. It can define protection for threatened ecosystems, but also some rights and duties (for example, <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a> and hunting rights).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>Law regarding species is more recent. It defines species that must be protected because they may be threatened by extinction. The U.S. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endangered_Species_Act" title="Endangered Species Act">Endangered Species Act</a> is an example of an attempt to address the "law and species" issue.</li>
<li>Laws regarding gene pools are only about a century old.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Domestication and plant breeding methods are not new, but advances in genetic engineering have led to tighter laws covering distribution of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genetically_modified_organisms" title="Genetically modified organisms">genetically modified organisms</a>, gene <a href="/wiki/Patent" title="Patent">patents</a> and process patents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup> Governments struggle to decide whether to focus on for example, genes, genomes, or organisms and species.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li></ul>
<p>Uniform approval for use of biodiversity as a legal standard has not been achieved, however. Bosselman argues that biodiversity should not be used as a legal standard, claiming that the remaining areas of scientific uncertainty cause unacceptable administrative waste and increase litigation without promoting preservation goals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup>
</p><p>India passed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biological_Diversity_Act" title="Biological Diversity Act">Biological Diversity Act</a> in 2002 for the conservation of biological diversity in India. The Act also provides mechanisms for equitable sharing of benefits from the use of traditional biological resources and knowledge.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Analytical_limits">Analytical limits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Analytical limits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxonomic_and_size_relationships">Taxonomic and size relationships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Taxonomic and size relationships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Less than 1% of all species that have been described have been studied beyond simply noting their existence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup> The vast majority of Earth's species are microbial. Contemporary biodiversity physics is "firmly fixated on the visible [macroscopic] world".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup> For example, microbial life is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metabolically" title="Metabolically">metabolically</a> and environmentally more diverse than multicellular life (see e.g., <a href="/wiki/Extremophile" title="Extremophile">extremophile</a>). "On the tree of life, based on analyses of small-subunit <a href="/wiki/Ribosomal_RNA" title="Ribosomal RNA">ribosomal RNA</a>, visible life consists of barely noticeable twigs. The inverse relationship of size and population recurs higher on the evolutionary ladder—to a first approximation, all multicellular species on Earth are insects".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Decline_in_insect_populations" title="Decline in insect populations">Insect extinction</a> rates are high—supporting the Holocene extinction hypothesis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Diversity_study_.28botany.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Diversity_study_(botany)">Diversity study (botany)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Diversity study (botany)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The number of morphological attributes that can be scored for diversity study is generally limited and prone to environmental influences; thereby reducing the fine resolution required to ascertain the phylogenetic relationships. DNA based markers- microsatellites otherwise known as <i>simple sequence repeats</i> (SSR) were therefore used for the diversity studies of certain species and their wild relatives.
</p><p>In the case of <a href="/wiki/Cowpea" title="Cowpea">cowpea</a>, a study conducted to assess the level of genetic diversity in cowpea germplasm and related wide species, where the relatedness among various taxa was compared, primers useful for classification of taxa identified, and the origin and phylogeny of cultivated cowpea classified show that SSR markers are useful in validating with species classification and revealing the center of diversity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-208"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-208">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFStokstad2019">Stokstad, Erik (6 May 2019). <a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1126%2Fscience.aax9287" rel="nofollow">"Landmark analysis documents the alarming global decline of nature"</a>. <i>Science</i>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1126%2Fscience.aax9287" rel="nofollow">10.1126/science.aax9287</a></span>. <q>For the first time at a global scale, the report has ranked the causes of damage. Topping the list, changes in land use—principally agriculture—that have destroyed habitat. Second, hunting and other kinds of exploitation. These are followed by climate change, pollution, and invasive species, which are being spread by trade and other activities. Climate change will likely overtake the other threats in the next decades, the authors note. Driving these threats are the growing human population, which has doubled since 1970 to 7.6 billion, and consumption. (Per capita of use of materials is up 15% over the past 5 decades.)</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Science&amp;rft.atitle=Landmark+analysis+documents+the+alarming+global+decline+of+nature&amp;rft.date=2019-05-06&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1126%2Fscience.aax9287&amp;rft.aulast=Stokstad&amp;rft.aufirst=Erik&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fdoi.org%2F10.1126%252Fscience.aax9287&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABiodiversity"></span></span>
</li>
